Spectrometry Quantification of Analytes</h3><div class="content"><p class="">Stable isotope dilution liquid chromatography with on-line tandem mass spectrometry (LC-MS/MS) was used for the quantification of plasma and tissue TMAO, choline, and betaine as previously described (<span class="bibRef"><a href="javascript:void(0);" id="back-bib31" class="layerTrigger layerTriggerClick">Wang et al., 2011</a><span class="hoverLayer refLayer"><span class="closeBtn" role="button" tabindex="0" aria-label="close window">x</span><span class="refTitle">Gut flora metabolism of phosphatidylcholine </span><span class="refSeriesTitle">Nature</span>. <span class="refSeriesDate">2011</span>;
        <span class="refSeriesVolume">472</span>: <span class="refPages">57&ndash;63</span><br></br><span class="reference"><a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=e_1_5_1_2_31_2&amp;dbid=16&amp;doi=10.1016/j.cell.2015.11.055&amp;key=10.1038%2Fnature09922&amp;cf=" onclick="newWindow(this.href);return false">CrossRef</a> | <a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=e_1_5_1_2_31_2&amp;dbid=8&amp;doi=10.1016/j.cell.2015.11.055&amp;key=21475195&amp;cf=" onclick="newWindow(this.href);return false">PubMed</a> | <a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=e_1_5_1_2_31_2&amp;dbid=137438953472&amp;doi=10.1016/j.cell.2015.11.055&amp;key=2-s2.0-79953733693&amp;cf=" onclick="newWindow(this.href);return false">Scopus (709)</a></span><a href="#references" class="allReferencesLink">See all References</a></span></span>, <span class="bibRef"><a href="javascript:void(0);" id="back-bib32" class="layerTrigger layerTriggerClick">Wang et al., 2014a</a><span class="hoverLayer refLayer"><span class="closeBtn" role="button" tabindex="0" aria-label="close window">x</span><span class="refTitle">Measurement of trimethylamine-N-oxide by stable isotope dilution liquid chromatography tandem mass spectrometry. </span><span class="refAuthors">Wang, Z., Levison, B.S., Hazen, J.E., Donahue, L., Li, X.M.,  and Hazen, S.L. </span><span class="refSeriesTitle">Anal.         <span class="refSeriesVolume">455</span>: <span class="refPages">35&ndash;40</span><br></br><span class="reference"><a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=e_1_5_1_2_32_2&amp;dbid=16&amp;doi=10.1016/j.cell.2015.11.055&amp;key=10.1016%2Fj.ab.2014.03.016&amp;cf=" onclick="newWindow(this.href);return false">CrossRef</a> | <a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=e_1_5_1_2_32_2&amp;dbid=8&amp;doi=10.1016/j.cell.2015.11.055&amp;key=24704102&amp;cf=" onclick="newWindow(this.href);return false">PubMed</a> | <a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=e_1_5_1_2_32_2&amp;dbid=137438953472&amp;doi=10.1016/j.cell.2015.11.055&amp;key=2-s2.0-84899457029&amp;cf=" onclick="newWindow(this.href);return false">Scopus (12)</a></span><a href="#references" class="allReferencesLink">See all References</a></span></span>). Samples used for TMA quantification were acidified prior to storage, and d9-TMA was used as an internal standard for quantification by LC/MS/MS. Liver cholesterol was quantified by gas chromatography/mass spectrometry (GC/MS) (<span class="bibRef"><a href="javascript:void(0);" id="back-bib31" class="layerTrigger layerTriggerClick">Wang et al., 2011</a><span class="hoverLayer refLayer"><span class="closeBtn" role="button" tabindex="0" aria-label="close window">x</span><span class="refTitle">Gut flora metabolism of phosphatidylcholine promotes cardiovascular disease. </span><span class="refAuthors">Wang, Z., Klipfell, E., Bennett, B.J., Koeth, R., Levison, B.S., Dugar, B., Feldstein, A.E., Britt, E.B., Fu, X., Chung, Y.M. et al. </span><span class="refSeriesTitle">Nature</span>. <span class="refSeriesDate">2011</span>;

class="sectionTitle">Determination of TMA Lyase Activity</h3><div class="content"><p class="">TMA lyase activity was typically quantified by incubating (for 1016 hr) the indicated enzyme source (intact cell [optical density at 600 nm, or OD<sub>600 nm</sub>, ~1.0], cell lysate [3 mg protein], or purified protein [30 g]) with the indicated co-factors in the presence or absence of DMB (2 mM), unless otherwise stated. Reactions were initiated by the addition of d9-labeled substrate (100 M, unless otherwise indicated) in gas-tight reaction vials at 37C. d9-TMA production was quantified by LC/MS/MS. Complete details can be found in the <span class="externalFile"><a href="/cms/attachment/2043164566/2055768690/mmc1.pdf" class="layerTrigger layerTriggerClick fileLink" id="back-mmc1">Supplemental Experimental Procedures</a><span class="externalFileLayer"><span class="closeBtn" role="button" tabindex="0" aria-label="close window">x</span><span class="download"><a href="/cms/attachment/2043164566/2055768690/mmc1.pdf"><img src="/templates/jsp/_style2/_marlin/images/icon_pdf.gif" alt="pdf icon"></img>Download

Contributions</option><option value="#app2" class="level_1">Supplemental Information</option><option value="#cebib0010" class="level_1">References</option></select><h3 class="sectionTitle">Cloning and Expression of <em>cutC/cutD</em>, <em>cntA/cntB</em>, and <em>yeaW/yeaX</em></h3><div class="content"><p class=""><em>P. mirabilis</em> (ATCC 29906) whole-genome sequence, contig00092 (ACLE01000068.1), was used to acquire the nucleotide sequence of <em>cutC</em> (locus tag: HMPREF0693_2863), <em>cutD</em> (locus tag: HMPREF0693_2862), and the 104 bases of intergenic DNA between <em>cutC</em> and <em>cutD</em>. The open reading frames (ORFs) for <em>cutC/D</em> were codon optimized, synthesized contiguously by GenScript (<a href="http://www.genscript.com" target="_blank">http://www.genscript.com</a>), and then cloned into pBAD (Invitrogen) and transformed into <em>E. coli</em> Top10 cells (Invitrogen). For expression of amino-terminal 8x-His-tagged CutC and carboxy-terminal Strep-Tag II-tagged CutD, the codon-optimized <em>cutC-</em>intergenic region<em>-cutD</em> from <em>P. mirabilis</em> was PCR amplified and cloned in-frame into the plasmid pGK::nucMCS that was isolated from <em>L. lactis</em> (ATCC 8731) behind an N-terminal 8x-His tag and in front of a Strep-tag II affinity tag. Sequence-verified clones were transformed into <em>E. coli</em> Stellar cells (Clontech). The ORFs for <em>Desulfovibrio alaskensis</em> G20 <em>cutC/D</em> genes (Ddes_3282 and Ddes_1357, respectively) and their associated intergenic region were codon optimized for expression in <em>E. coli</em> and synthesized by GenScript, for cloning into pUC57. Constitutive expression of the <em>D. alaskensis</em> G20 CutC/D proteins in <em>E. coli</em> Top10 cells (Invitrogen) was performed using the synthetic <em>em7</em> constitutive bacterial promoter with ribosome-binding site, as described in the <span class="externalFile"><a href="/cms/attachment/2043164566/2055768690/mmc1.pdf" class="layerTrigger layerTriggerClick fileLink" id="back-mmc1">Supplemental Experimental Procedures</a><span class="externalFileLayer"><span class="closeBtn" role="button" tabindex="0" aria-label="close window">x</span><span class="download"><a href="/cms/attachment/2043164566/2055768690/mmc1.pdf"><img src="/templates/jsp/_style2/_marlin/images/icon_pdf.gif" alt="pdf icon"></img>Download
                    (.35 MB
    )
                    
                </a></span><br></br><br></br><span class="label">Document S1. Supplemental Experimental Procedures and Tables S1S4</span></span></span><span class="hidden crossref-label"><span class="mmc1">Supplemental Experimental Procedures</span></span>. The genes for y<em>eaW/yeaX</em> were cloned from <em>E. coli</em> K-12 DH10B genomic DNA by PCR, inserted into a modified pET22 vector backbone, and expressed in <em>E. coli</em> BL21(DE3) (Invitrogen) (<span class="bibRef"><a href="javascript:void(0);" id="back-bib15" class="layerTrigger layerTriggerClick">Koeth et al., 2014</a><span class="hoverLayer refLayer"><span class="closeBtn" role="button" tabindex="0" aria-label="close window">x</span><span class="refTitle">?-Butyrobetaine is a proatherogenic intermediate in gut microbial metabolism of L-carnitine to TMAO. </span><span class="refAuthors">Koeth, R.A., Levison, B.S., Culley, M.K., Buffa, J.A., Wang, Z., Gregory, J.C., Org, E., Wu, Y., Li, L., Smith, J.D. et al. </span><span class="refSeriesTitle">Cell Metab.</span> <span class="refSeriesDate">2014</span>;
        <span class="refSeriesVolume">20</span>: <span class="refPages">799&ndash;812</span><br></br><span class="reference"><a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=e_1_5_1_2_15_2&amp;dbid=4&amp;doi=10.1016/j.cell.2015.11.055&amp;key=10.1016%2Fj.cmet.2014.10.006&amp;cf=abstract&amp;site=cell-site" onclick="newWindow(this.href);return false">Abstract</a> | <a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=e_1_5_1_2_15_2&amp;dbid=4&amp;doi=10.1016/j.cell.2015.11.055&amp;key=10.1016%2Fj.cmet.2014.10.006&amp;cf=fulltext&amp;site=cell-site" onclick="newWindow(this.href);return false">Full Text</a> | <a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=e_1_5_1_2_15_2&amp;dbid=4&amp;doi=10.1016/j.cell.2015.11.055&amp;key=10.1016%2Fj.cmet.2014.10.006&amp;cf=pdf&amp;site=cell-site" onclick="newWindow(this.href);return false">Full Text PDF</a> | <a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=e_1_5_1_2_15_2&amp;dbid=8&amp;doi=10.1016/j.cell.2015.11.055&amp;key=25440057&amp;cf=" onclick="newWindow(this.href);return false">PubMed</a> | <a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=e_1_5_1_2_15_2&amp;dbid=137438953472&amp;doi=10.1016/j.cell.2015.11.055&amp;key=2-s2.0-84910129274&amp;cf=" onclick="newWindow(this.href);return false">Scopus (20)</a></span><a href="#references" class="allReferencesLink">See all References</a></span></span><span class="hidden crossref-label"><span class="bib15">Koeth et al., 2014</span></span>). For expression of 8x-His-tagged YeaW and 8x-His-tagged YeaX proteins, the relevant genes were cloned in-frame behind an 8x-His-tag in <em>E. coli</em> BL21(DE3). <em>CntA</em>/<em>cntB</em> genes from <em>Acinetobacter baumannii</em> (ATCC 19606) (<span class="bibRef"><a href="javascript:void(0);" id="back-bib36" class="layerTrigger layerTriggerClick">Zhu et al., 2014</a><span class="hoverLayer refLayer"><span class="closeBtn" role="button" tabindex="0" aria-label="close window">x</span><span class="refTitle">Carnitine metabolism to trimethylamine by an unusual Rieske-type oxygenase from human microbiota. </span><span class="refAuthors">Zhu, Y., Jameson, E., Crosatti, M., Schfer, H., Rajakumar, K., Bugg, T.D.,  and Chen, Y. </span><span class="refSeriesTitle">Proc. Induction Conditions for Recombinant TMA Lyases</h3><div class="content"><p class="">Recombinant clones transformed in <em>E. coli</em> Top10 and BL21(DE3) were grown in Luria broth (LB) medium with 100 g/ml ampicillin, and arabinose or isopropyl -D-1-thiogalactopyranoside (IPTG) was added at a final concentration of 0.2% or 0.4 mM for induction of TMA lyase subunits constructed in pBAD or pET vectors, respectively. The <em>cutC</em>/<em>D</em> recombinant clones in the pGK or pUC57 vectors were grown in LB medium with erythromycin (250 g/ml) or ampicillin (100 g/ml), respectively, at 37C overnight to constitutively express the targeted TMA lyase subunit. Further details can be found in the <span class="externalFile"><a href="/cms/attachment/2043164566/2055768690/mmc1.pdf" class="layerTrigger layerTriggerClick fileLink" id="back-mmc1">Supplemental Experimental Procedures</a><span class="externalFileLayer"><span class="closeBtn" role="button" tabindex="0" aria-label="close window">x</span><span class="download"><a href="/cms/attachment/2043164566/2055768690/mmc1.pdf"><img src="/templates/jsp/_style2/_marlin/images/icon_pdf.gif" alt="pdf icon"></img>Download

Mouse Cecum, and Human Feces TMA Lyase Sample Preparation</h3><div class="content"><p class="">Mouse cecum from C57BL/6J <em>Apoe</em><sup><em>-/-</em></sup> mice or human feces was gently homogenized, followed by centrifugation under argon atmosphere. The upper phase was collected followed by centrifugation under argon blanket. The bottom pellet was collected, resuspended, and used as intact bacterium cell suspensions under either nitrogen or argon atmosphere in gas-tight vials. Lysates of bacteria were generated either by French press using argon gas or by homogenization with 100-m glass beads using a TissueLyser II (QIAGEN) kept within an argon- or a nitrogen-filled chamber.</p></div></section><section id="sec4.10" class=""><select name="heading" class="sectionHeading" onChange="window.location.hash=this.value; return false;"><option value="" Studies</h3><div class="content"><p class="">Bacterial DNA was isolated from mouse cecum, and 16S rRNA gene V4 hypervariable regions were amplified, pyrosequenced, assigned into different taxa, and analyzed as previously described (<span class="bibRef"><a href="javascript:void(0);" id="back-bib12" class="layerTrigger layerTriggerClick">Gregory et al., 2015</a><span class="hoverLayer refLayer"><span class="closeBtn" role="button" tabindex="0" aria-label="close window">x</span><span class="refTitle">Transmission of atherosclerosis susceptibility with gut microbial transplantation.         <span class="refSeriesVolume">290</span>: <span class="refPages">5647&ndash;5660</span><br></br><span class="reference"><a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=e_1_5_1_2_12_2&amp;dbid=16&amp;doi=10.1016/j.cell.2015.11.055&amp;key=10.1074%2Fjbc.M114.618249&amp;cf=" onclick="newWindow(this.href);return false">CrossRef</a> | <a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=e_1_5_1_2_12_2&amp;dbid=8&amp;doi=10.1016/j.cell.2015.11.055&amp;key=25550161&amp;cf=" onclick="newWindow(this.href);return false">PubMed</a> | <a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=e_1_5_1_2_12_2&amp;dbid=137438953472&amp;doi=10.1016/j.cell.2015.11.055&amp;key=2-s2.0-84923913674&amp;cf=" onclick="newWindow(this.href);return false">Scopus (11)</a></span><a href="#references" class="allReferencesLink">See all References</a></span></span>, <span class="bibRef"><a href="javascript:void(0);" id="back-bib14" class="layerTrigger layerTriggerClick">Koeth et al., 2013</a><span class="hoverLayer refLayer"><span class="closeBtn" role="button" tabindex="0" aria-label="close window">x</span><span class="refTitle">Intestinal microbiota metabolism of L-carnitine, a nutrient in red meat, promotes atherosclerosis. </span><span class="refAuthors">Koeth, R.A., Wang, Z., Levison, B.S., Buffa, J.A., Org, E., Sheehy, B.T., Britt, E.B., Fu, X., Wu, Y., Li, L. et al. </span><span class="refSeriesTitle">Nat.         <span class="refSeriesVolume">19</span>: <span class="refPages">576&ndash;585</span><br></br><span class="reference"><a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=e_1_5_1_2_14_2&amp;dbid=16&amp;doi=10.1016/j.cell.2015.11.055&amp;key=10.1038%2Fnm.3145&amp;cf=" onclick="newWindow(this.href);return false">CrossRef</a> | <a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=e_1_5_1_2_14_2&amp;dbid=8&amp;doi=10.1016/j.cell.2015.11.055&amp;key=23563705&amp;cf=" onclick="newWindow(this.href);return false">PubMed</a> | <a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=e_1_5_1_2_14_2&amp;dbid=137438953472&amp;doi=10.1016/j.cell.2015.11.055&amp;key=2-s2.0-84877331372&amp;cf=" onclick="newWindow(this.href);return false">Scopus (358)</a></span><a href="#references" class="allReferencesLink">See all References</a></span></span>). We conducted a principal-component analysis (PCA) using MarkerView Software (AB SCIEX) to compare the effects of different diets and DMB exposure on microbiota composition.</p></div></section><section Contributions</option><option value="#app2" class="level_1">Supplemental Information</option><option value="#cebib0010" class="level_1">References</option></select><h3 class="sectionTitle">Statistical Analyses</h3><div class="content"><p class="">We analyzed data using the Students t test and ANOVA, followed by post hoc t test with Holm-Bonferroni correction, to compare differences in mean value between different groups for most studies, as indicated. Pearsons correlation was used to calculate the association between two variables after demonstration of normal distribution of data. For all statistical tests, p &lt; 0.05 was considered significant.</p></div></section></div></section><section id="sec5" class="acknowledgement"><select name="heading" class="sectionHeading" Contributions</h2><div class="content"><p class="">Z.W. helped with the design, performance, and analyses of all studies and the drafting of the manuscript. A.B.R., J.A.D., X.G., Y.H., M.Z.-D., A.J.D., and X.F. assisted in gene cloning, protein purification, choline transport, and TMA lyase activity assay. All authors critically reviewed the manuscript.</p></div></section></div><section id="Acknowledgments"><select name="heading" class="sectionHeading" onChange="window.location.hash=this.value; return
